chapter xlii an authentic ghost story for some remarkable reason ghostly legends were uncommonly rife about this time among the servant on simon_legree place
it was whisperingly asserted that footsteps in the dead of night had been heard descending the garret stairs and patrolling the house
in vain the door of the upper entry had been locked the ghost either carried a duplicate key in its pocket or availed itself of a ghost immemorial privilege of coming through the keyhole and promenaded as before with a freedom that was alarming
authorities were somewhat divided as to the outward form of the spirit owing to a custom quite prevalent among negroes and for aught we know among whites too of invariably shutting the eye and covering up head under blankets petticoats or whatever else might come in use for a shelter on these occasions
of course as everybody knows when the bodily eye are thus out of the lists the spiritual eye are uncommonly vivacious and perspicuous and therefore there were abundance of full length portraits of the ghost abundantly sworn and testified to which as is often the case with portraits agreed with each other in no particular except the common family peculiarity of the ghost tribe the wearing of a white sheet
the poor soul were not versed in ancient history and did not know that shakspeare had authenticated this costume by telling how the sheeted dead did squeak and gibber in the streets of rome
and therefore their all hitting upon this is a striking fact in pneumatology which we recommend to the attention of spiritual media generally
be it as it may we have private reasons for knowing that a tall figure in a white sheet did walk at the most approved ghostly hour around the simon_legree premises pass out the door glide about the house disappear at intervals and reappearing pass up the silent stairway into that fatal garret and that in the morning the entry door were all found shut and locked as firm as ever
simon_legree could not help overhearing this whispering and it was all the more exciting to him from the pains that were taken to conceal it from him
he drank more brandy than usual held up his head briskly and swore louder than ever in the daytime but he had bad dreams and the visions of his head on his bed were anything but agreeable
the night after tom_loker body had been carried away he rode to the next town for a carouse and had a high one
hamlet act i scene lines got home late and tired locked his door took out the key and went to bed
after all let a man take what pains he may to hush it down a human soul is an awful ghostly unquiet possession for a bad man to have
who knows all its awful perhapses those shudderings and tremblings which it can no more live down than it can outlive its own eternity
what a fool is he who locks his door to keep out spirit who has in his own bosom a spirit he dares not meet alone whose voice smothered far down and piled over with mountains of earthliness is yet like the forewarning trumpet of doom
but simon_legree locked his door and set a chair against it he set a night lamp at the head of his bed and put his pistols there
he examined the catches and fastenings of the window and then swore he didnt care for the devil and all his angels and went to sleep
who knows the metes and bounds of it well he slept for he was tired slept soundly but finally there came over his sleep a shadow a horror an apprehension of something dreadful hanging over him
he heard a confused noise of screams and groanings and with it all he knew he was asleep and he struggled to wake himself
it was his mother shroud he thought but misse_cassy had it holding it up and showing it to him he was half awake
he was sure something was coming into his room he knew the door was opening but he could not stir hand or foot
at last he turned with a start the door was open and he saw a hand putting out his light it was a cloudy misty moonlight and there he saw it something white gliding in
it stood still by his bed a cold hand touched his a voice said three time in a low fearful whisper come
he heard the still rustle of its ghostly garments come come and while he lay sweating with terror he knew not when or how the thing was gone
he sprang out of bed and pulled at the door it was shut and locked and the man fell down in a swoon
after this simon_legree became a harder drinker than ever before he no longer drank cautiously prudently but imprudently and recklessly there were reports around the country soon after that he was sick and dying
excess had brought on that frightful disease that seems to throw the lurid shadows of a coming retribution back into the present life
none could bear the horrors of that sick room when he raved and screamed and spoke of sights which almost stopped the blood of those who heard him and at his dying bed stood a stern white inexorable figure saying come
by a singular coincidence on the very night that this vision appeared to simon_legree the house door was found open in the morning and some of the negroes had seen two white figures gliding down the avenue towards the high road
it was near sunrise when misse_cassy and emmeline paused for a moment in a little knot of trees near the town
come come misse_cassy was dressed after the manner of the creole spanish lady wholly in black a small black bonnet on her head covered by a veil thick with embroidery concealed her face
it had been agreed that in their escape she was to personate the character of a creole lady and emmeline that of her servant
brought up from early life in connection with the highest society the language movements and air of misse_cassy were all in agreement with this idea and she had still enough remaining with her of a once splendid wardrobe and sets of jewels to enable her to personate the thing to advantage
she stopped in the outskirts of the town where she had noticed trunks for sale and purchased a handsome one this
and accordingly thus escorted by a boy wheeling her trunk and emmeline behind her carrying her carpet bag and sundry bundles she made her appearance at the small tavern like a lady of consideration
she requested the man to send along with her the first person that struck her after her arrival was george_harris mr_shelby who was staying there awaiting the next boat
misse_cassy had remarked the young man from her loophole in the garret and seen him bear away the body of tom_loker and observed with secret exultation his rencontre with simon_legree
subsequently she had gathered from the conversations she had overheard among the negroes as she glided about in her ghostly disguise after nightfall who he was and in what relation he stood to tom_loker
she therefore felt an immediate accession of confidence when she found that he was like herself awaiting the next boat misse_cassy air and manner address and evident command of money prevented any rising disposition to suspicion in the hotel
people never inquire too closely into those who are fair on the main point of paying well a thing which misse_cassy had foreseen when she provided herself with money
in the edge of the evening a boat was heard coming along and george_harris mr_shelby handed misse_cassy aboard with the politeness which comes naturally to every kentuckian and exerted himself to provide her with a good state room
misse_cassy kept her room and bed on pretext of illness during the whole time they were on red river and was waited on with obsequious devotion by her attendant

behold therefore the whole party safely transferred to the good steamer cincinnati and sweeping up the river under a powerful head of steam

misse_cassy health was much better he could not keep himself from looking at her and watching her perpetually misse_cassy became uneasy
she began to think that he suspected something and finally resolved to throw herself entirely on his generosity and intrusted him with her whole history
george_harris was heartily disposed to sympathize with any one who had escaped from simon_legree plantation a place that he could not remember or speak of with patience and with the courageous disregard of consequences which is characteristic of his age and state he assured her that he would do all in his power to protect and bring them through
the next state room to misse_cassy was occupied by a french lady named madame_de_thoux who was accompanied by a fine little daughter a child of some twelve summers
this lady having gathered from george_harris conversation that he was from kentucky seemed evidently disposed to cultivate his acquaintance in which design she was seconded by the graces of her little girl who was about as pretty a plaything as ever diverted the weariness of a fortnight trip on a steamboat
george_harris chair was often placed at her state room door and misse_cassy as she sat upon the guards could hear their conversation
madame_de_thoux was very minute in her inquiries as to kentucky where she said she had resided in a former period of her life
george_harris discovered to his surprise that her former residence must have been in his own vicinity and her inquiries showed a knowledge of people and thing in his vicinity that was perfectly surprising to him

there is an old fellow of that name life not far from my father place said george_harris we never have had much intercourse with him though

he is my brother she said madame said george_harris with a strong accent of surprise yes said madame_de_thoux lifting her head proudly and wiping her tear mr_shelby george_harris is my brother

what sort of a girl said madame_de_thoux eagerly a treasure said george_harris a beautiful intelligent amiable girl
very pious my mother had brought her up and trained her as carefully almost as a daughter she could read and write embroider and sew beautifully and was a beautiful singer

father would never tell mother what he gave for her but the other day in looking over his old paper we came across the bill of sale
george_harris sat with his back to misse_cassy and did not see the absorbed expression of her countenance as he was giving these details

though neither of them could conjecture what was the cause of misse_cassy fainting still they made all the tumult which is proper in such case george_harris upsetting a wash pitcher and breaking two tumblers in the warmth of his humanity and various lady in the cabin hearing that somebody had fainted crowded the state room door and kept out all the air they possibly could so that on the whole everything was done that could be expected

she felt as sure in that hour that god had had mercy on her and that she should see her daughter as she did months afterwards when but we anticipate
george_harris was wide awake now and so was madame_de_thoux poor misse_cassy perhaps you cannot but chapter xliii results the rest of our story is soon told
george_harris mr_shelby interested as any other young man might be by the romance of the incident no less than by feeling of humanity was at the pains to send to misse_cassy the bill of sale of eliza_harris whose date and name all corresponded with her own knowledge of fact and felt no doubt upon her mind as to the identity of her child
madame_de_thoux and she thus drawn together by the singular coincidence of their fortunes proceeded immediately to canada and began a tour of inquiry among the stations where the numerous fugitives from slavery are located
at amherstberg they found the missionary with whom george_harris and eliza_harris had taken shelter on their first arrival in canada and through him were enabled to trace the family to montreal
it remained now only for her to trace out the path of the fugitives george_harris and eliza_harris had now been five year free
george_harris had found constant occupation in the shop of a worthy machinist where he had been earning a competent support for his family which in the mean time had been increased by the addition of another daughter
the worthy pastor of the station in amherstberg where george_harris had first landed was so much interested in the statements of madame_de_thoux and misse_cassy that he yielded to the solicitations of the former to accompany them to montreal in their search she bearing all the expense of the expedition
little harry a fine bright boy had been put to a good school and was making rapid proficiency in knowledge the scene now changes to a small neat tenement in the outskirts of montreal the time evening
in one corner of the room was a table covered with a green cloth where was an open writing desk pens paper and over it a shelf of well selected book
a cheerful fire blazes on the hearth a tea table covered with a snowy cloth stands prepared for the evening meal this was george_harris study
the same zeal for self improvement which led him to steal the much coveted arts of reading and writing amid all the toil and discouragements of his early life still led him to devote all his leisure time to self cultivation
at this present time he is seated at the table making notes from a volume of the family library he has been reading

and little eliza_harris seconds the effort by toddling up to her father and trying to pull the book out of his hand and install herself on his knee as a substitute

her form a little fuller her air more matronly than of yore but evidently contented and happy as woman need be

now if the truth must be told the honest pastor had arranged a little programme according to which this affair was to develop itself and on the way up all had very cautiously and prudently exhorted each other not to let thing out except according to previous arrangement
what was the good man consternation therefore just as he had motioned to the lady to be seated and was taking out his pocket handkerchief to wipe his mouth so as to proceed to his introductory speech in good order when madame_de_thoux upset the whole plan by throwing her arm around george_harris neck and letting all out at once by saying george_harris

misse_cassy had seated herself more composedly and would have carried on her part very well had not little eliza_harris suddenly appeared before her in exact shape and form every outline and curl just as her daughter was when she saw her last

in fact it was a troublesome matter to do up exactly in proper order but the good pastor at last succeeded in getting everybody quiet and delivering the speech with which he had intended to open the exercises and in which at last he succeeded so well that his whole audience were sobbing about him in a manner that ought to satisfy any orator ancient or modern
there are some feeling so agitated and tumultuous that they can find rest only by being poured into the bosom of almighty love and then rising up the new found family embraced each other with a holy trust in him who from such peril and dangers and by such unknown way had brought them together
they knelt together and the good man prayed for the note book of a missionary among the canadian fugitives contains truth stranger than fiction
how can it be otherwise when a system prevails which whirls family and scatters their members as the wind whirls and scatters the leaves of autumn
these shores of refuge like the eternal shore often unite again in glad communion heart that for long year have mourned each other as lost
and affecting beyond expression is the earnestness with which every new arrival among them is met if perchance it may bring tidings of mother sister child or wife still lost to view in the shadows of slavery
deeds of heroism are wrought here more than those of romance when defying torture and braving death itself the fugitive voluntarily threads his way back to the terrors and perils of that dark land that he may bring out his sister or mother or wife
one young man of whom a missionary has told us twice re captured and suffering shameful stripes for his heroism had escaped again and in a letter which we heard read tells his friend that he is going back a third time that he may at last bring away his sister
my good sir is this man a hero or a criminal would not you do as much for your sister and can you blame him
but to return to our friend whom we left wiping their eye and recovering themselves from too great and sudden a joy
they are now seated around the social board and are getting decidedly companionable only that misse_cassy who keeps little eliza_harris on her lap occasionally squeezes the little thing in a manner that rather astonishes her and obstinately refuses to have her mouth stuffed with cake to the extent the little one desires alleging what the child rather wonders at that she has got something better than cake and doesnt want it
and indeed in two or three day such a change has passed over misse_cassy that our readers would scarcely know her
she seemed to sink at once into the bosom of the family and take the little one into her heart as something for which it long had waited
indeed her love seemed to flow more naturally to the little eliza_harris than to her own daughter for she was the exact image and body of the child whom she had lost
the despairing haggard expression of her face had given way to one of gentle trust the little one was a flowery bond between mother and daughter through whom grew up acquaintanceship and affection
eliza_harris steady consistent piety regulated by the constant reading of the sacred word made her a proper guide for the shattered and wearied mind of her mother
misse_cassy yielded at once and with her whole soul to every good influence and became a devout and tender christian after a day or two madame_de_thoux told her brother more particularly of her affairs

the death of her husband had left her an ample fortune which she generously offered to share with the family then i can do all the rest
on mature deliberation it was decided that the whole family should go for some year to france whither they sailed carrying emmeline with them
the good looks of the latter won the affection of the first mate of the vessel and shortly after entering the port she became his wife
george_harris remained four year at a french university and applying himself with an unintermitted zeal obtained a very thorough education
political troubles in france at last led the family again to seek an asylum in this country george_harris feeling and views as an educated man may be best expressed in a letter to one of his friend
true as you have said to me i might mingle in the circles of the whites in this country my shade of color is so slight and that of my wife and family scarce perceptible
i feel somewhat at a loss as to my future course well perhaps on sufferance i might but to tell you the truth i have no wish to
my sympathies are not for my father race but for my mother to him i was no more than a fine dog or horse to my poor heart broken mother
i was a child and though i never saw her after the cruel sale that separated us till she died yet
when i think of all she suffered of my own early sufferings of the distresses and struggles of my heroic wife of my sister sold in the new orleans slave market though
i hope to have no unchristian sentiments yet i may be excused for saying i have no wish to pass for an american or to identify myself with them
it is with the oppressed enslaved african race that i cast in my lot and if i wished anything i would wish myself two shades darker rather than one lighter
i know she always loved me dearly i know it by my own heart the desire and yearning of my soul is for an african nationality
i want a people that shall have a tangible separate existence of its own and where am i to look for it
the race that formed the character of the haytiens was a worn out effeminate one and of course the subject race will be centuries in rising to anything
not in hayti for in hayti they had nothing to start with a stream cannot rise above its fountain where then shall i look
on the shores of africa i see a republic a republic formed of picked man who by energy and self educating force have in many case individually raised themselves above a condition of slavery
having gone through a preparatory stage of feebleness this republic has at last become an acknowledged nation on the face of the earth acknowledged by both france and england
there it is my wish to go and find myself a people i am aware now that i shall have you all against me but before you strike hear me
i have noted the struggle between abolitionist and colonizationist and have received some impressions as a distant spectator which could never have occurred to me as a participator
i grant that this liberia may have subserved all sort of purposes by being played off in the hand of our oppressors against us
during my stay in france i have followed up with intense interest the history of my people in america doubtless the scheme may have been used in unjustifiable way as a means of retarding our emancipation
but the question to me is is there not a god above all man schemes may he not have over ruled their designs and founded for us a nation by them
a nation starts now with all the great problems of republican life and civilization wrought out to its hand it has not to discover but only to apply
let us then all take hold together with all our might and see what we can do with this new enterprise and the whole splendid continent of africa opens before us and our child
our nation shall roll the tide of civilization and christianity along its shores and plant there mighty republics that growing with the rapidity of tropical vegetation shall be for all coming ages
in these day a nation is born in a day do you say that i am deserting my enslaved brethren
i think not if i forget them one hour one moment of my life so may god forget me but what can i do for them here
no not as an individual but let me go and form part of a nation which shall have a voice in the councils of nations and then we can speak
can i break their chains a nation has a right to argue remonstrate implore and present the cause of its race which
an individual has not if europe ever becomes a grand council of free nations as i trust in god it will if
there serfdom and all unjust and oppressive social inequalities are done away and if they as france and england have done acknowledge our position then in the great congress of nations we will make our appeal and present the cause of our enslaved and suffering race and it cannot be that free enlightened america will not then desire to wipe from her escutcheon that bar sinister which disgraces her among nations and is as truly a curse to her as to the enslaved
but you will tell me our race have equal rights to mingle in the american republic as the irishman the german the swede
we ought to be free to meet and mingle to rise by our individual worth without any consideration of caste or color and they who deny us this right are false to their own professed principles of human equality
granted they have we ought in particular to be allowed here we have more than the rights of common man we have the claim of an injured race for reparation
i think that the african race has peculiarities yet to be unfolded in the light of civilization and christianity which if not the same with those of the anglo saxon may prove to be morally of even a higher type
but then i do not want it i want a country a nation of my own to the anglo saxon race has been intrusted the destinies of the world during its pioneer period of struggle and conflict
to that mission its stern inflexible energetic elements were well adapted but as a christian i look for another era to arise
on its borders i trust we stand and the throes that now convulse the nations are to my hope but the birth pangs of an hour of universal peace and brotherhood
i trust that the development of africa is to be essentially a christian one if not a dominant and commanding race they are at least an affectionate magnanimous and forgiving one
having been called in the furnace of injustice and oppression they have need to bind closer to their heart that sublime doctrine of love and forgiveness through which alone they are to conquer which it is to be their mission to spread over the continent of africa
in myself i confess i am feeble for this full half the blood in my veins is the hot and hasty saxon but i have an eloquent preacher of the gospel ever by my side in the person of my beautiful wife
when i wander her gentler spirit ever restores me and keeps before my eye the christian calling and mission of our race
as a christian patriot as a teacher of christianity i go to my country my chosen my glorious africa and to her in my heart i sometimes apply those splendid word of prophecy whereas thou hast been forsaken and hated so that no man went through thee i will make thee an eternal excellence a joy of many generations
you will call me an enthusiast you will tell me that i have not well considered what i am undertaking
but i have considered and counted the cost i go to liberia not as an elysium of romance but as to a field of work
i expect to work with both hand to work hard to work against all sort of difficulties and discouragements and to work till i die
whatever you may think of my determination do not divorce me from your confidence and think that in whatever i do i act with a heart wholly given to my people
this is what i go for and in this i am quite sure i shall not be disappointed george_harris
george_harris with his wife child sister and mother embarked for africa some few weeks after if we are not mistaken the world will yet hear from him there
of our other characters we have nothing very particular to write except a word relating to miss_ophelia and topsy and a farewell chapter which we shall dedicate to george_harris mr_shelby
miss_ophelia took topsy home to vermont with her much to the surprise of the grave deliberative body whom a new englander recognizes under the term our folks
our folks at first thought it an odd and unnecessary addition to their well trained domestic establishment but so thoroughly efficient was miss_ophelia in her conscientious endeavor to do her duty by her lve that the child rapidly grew in grace and in favor with the family and neighborhood
at the age of womanhood she was by her own request baptized and became a member of the christian church in the place and showed so much intelligence activity and zeal and desire to do good in the world that she was at last recommended and approved as a missionary to one of the stations in africa and we have heard that the same activity and ingenuity which when a child made her so multiform and restless in her developments is now employed in a safer and wholesomer manner in teaching the child of her own country
p it will be a satisfaction to some mother also to state that some inquiries which were set on foot by madame_de_thoux have resulted recently in the discovery of misse_cassy son
being a young man of energy he had escaped some year before his mother and been received and educated by friend of the oppressed in the north
the liberator george_harris mr_shelby had written to his mother merely a line stating the day that she might expect him home
he will soon follow his family to africa chapter xliv of the death scene of his old friend he had not the heart to write
he had tried several time and only succeeded in half choking himself and invariably finished by tearing up the paper wiping his eye and rushing somewhere to get quiet
there was a pleased bustle all though the mr_shelby mansion that day in expectation of the arrival of young mas george_harris
mrs mr_shelby was seated in her comfortable parlor where a cheerful hickory fire was dispelling the chill of the late autumn evening
a supper table glittering with plate and cut glass was set out on whose arrangements our former friend old aunt_chloe was presiding
arrayed in a new calico dress with clean white apron and high well starched turban her black polished face glowing with satisfaction she lingered with needless punctiliousness around the arrangements of the table merely as an excuse for talking a little to her mistress
law now wont it look natural to him she said thar i set his plate just whar he likes it round by the fire
mas george_harris allers wants de warm seat go way why didnt sally get out de best tea pot de little new one mas r
george_harris got for missis christmas i ll have it out and missis has heard from mas george_harris she said inquiringly
yes aunt_chloe but only a line just to say he would be home tonight if he could that all didnt say nothing bout my old man pose
said aunt_chloe still fidgeting with the tea cups no he didnt he did not speak of anything aunt_chloe he said he would tell all when he got home
dont see for my part how white people gen lly can bar to hev to write thing much as they do writin such slow oneasy kind work
jes like mas george_harris he allers so ferce for tellin everything hisself i allers minded dat ar in mas george_harris
mrs mr_shelby smiled i a thinkin my old man wont know de boy and de baby lor she de biggest gal now good
she is too and peart polly is she out to the house now watchin de hoe cake i got jist de very pattern my old man liked so much a bakin
jist sich as i gin him the mornin he was took off lord bless us how i felt dat ar morning
she had felt uneasy ever since she received her son letter lest something should prove to be hidden behind the veil of silence which he had drawn
mrs mr_shelby sighed and felt a heavy weight on her heart at this allusion missis has got dem bills said aunt_chloe anxiously
yes aunt_chloe cause i wants to show my old man dem very bills de perfectioner gave me
thank you mas says i i would only my old man coming home and missis she cant do without me no longer
and say he aunt_chloe i wish you stay longer there jist what i telled him berry nice man dat mas jones was
aunt_chloe had pertinaciously insisted that the very bills in which her wages had been paid should be preserved to show her husband in memorial of her capability
and mrs mr_shelby had readily consented to humor her in the request he wont know polly my old man wont
law it five year since they tuck him she was a baby den couldnt but jist stand remember how tickled he used to be cause she would keep a fallin over when she sot out to walk
law a me the rattling of wheels now was heard mas george_harris said aunt_chloe starting to the window
mrs mr_shelby ran to the entry door and was folded in the arm of her son aunt_chloe stood anxiously straining her eye out into the darkness
said george_harris stopping compassionately and taking her hard black hand between both his i have given all my fortune to have brought him with me but he gone to a better country
poor aunt_chloe there was a passionate exclamation from mrs mr_shelby but aunt_chloe said nothing the party entered the supper room
thar said she gathering it up and holding it with a trembling hand to her mistress dont never want to see nor hear ont again
the money of which aunt_chloe was so proud was still lying on the table jist as i knewt would be sold and murdered on dem ar old plantation
mrs mr_shelby followed her softly and took one of her hand drew her down into a chair and sat down by her
aunt_chloe turned and was walking proudly out of the room my poor good aunt_chloe said she aunt_chloe leaned her head on her mistress shoulder and sobbed out missis
scuse me my heart broke dat all i know it is said mrs mr_shelby as her tear fell fast and i cannot heal it but lord_jesus can
he healeth the broken hearted and bindeth up their wounds there was a silence for some time and all wept together
at last george_harris sitting down beside the mourner took her hand and with simple pathos repeated the triumphant scene of her husband death and his last messages of love
about a month after this one morning all the servant of the mr_shelby estate were convened together in the great hall that ran through the house to hear a few word from their young master
to the surprise of all he appeared among them with a bundle of paper in his hand containing a certificate of freedom to every one on the place which he read successively and presented amid the sobs and tear and shouts of all present
many however pressed around him earnestly begging him not to send them away and with anxious face tendering back their free paper
we dont want to be no freer than we are we allers had all we wanted we dont want to leave de ole place and mas and missis and de rest
my good friend said george_harris as soon as he could get a silence there ll be no need for you to leave me
the place wants as many hand to work it as it did before we need the same about the house that we did before
but you are now free man and free woman i shall pay you wages for your work such as we shall agree on
the advantage is that in case of my getting in debt or dying thing that might happen you cannot now be taken up and sold
i expect to carry on the estate and to teach you what perhaps it will take you some time to learn how to use the rights i give you as free man and woman
i expect you to be good and willing to learn and i trust in god that i shall be faithful and willing to teach
an aged partriarchal negro who had grown gray and blind on the estate now rose and lifting his trembling hand said let us give thanks unto the lord
as all kneeled by one consent a more touching and hearty te deum never ascended to heaven though borne on the peal of organ bell and cannon than came from that honest old heart
on rising another struck up a methodist hymn of which the burden was the year of jubilee is come return ye ransomed sinners home
one thing more said george_harris as he stopped the congratulations of the throng you all remember our good old uncle tom_loker
george_harris here gave a short narration of the scene of his death and of his loving farewell to all on the place and added it was on his grave my friend that i resolved before god that i would never own another slave while it was possible to free him that nobody through me should ever run the risk of being parted from home and friend and dying on a lonely plantation as he died
so when you rejoice in your freedom think that you owe it to that good old soul and pay it back in kindness to his wife and child
think of your freedom every time you see uncle tom_loker cabin and let it be a memorial to put you all in mind to follow in his steps and be honest and faithful and christian as he was
and now my friend look up and thank god for the blessing of freedom chapter xlv concluding remarks
the writer has often been inquired of by correspondents from different part of the country whether this narrative is a true one and to these inquiries she will give one general answer
the separate incidents that compose the narrative are to a very great extent authentic occurring many of them either under her own observation or that of her personal friend
she or her friend have observed characters the counterpart of almost all that are here introduced and many of the sayings are word for word as heard herself or reported to her
the personal appearance of eliza_harris the character ascribed to her are sketches drawn from life the incorruptible fidelity piety and honesty of uncle tom_loker had more than one development to her personal knowledge
some of the most deeply tragic and romantic some of the most terrible incidents have also their parallels in reality the incident of the mother crossing the ohio river on the ice is a well known fact
the story of old prue in the second volume was an incident that fell under the personal observation of a brother of the writer then collecting clerk to a large mercantile house in new orleans
of him her brother thus wrote speaking of visiting his plantation on a collecting tour he actually made me feel of his fist which was like a blacksmith hammer or a nodule of iron telling me that it was calloused with knocking down nigger
when i left the plantation i drew a long breath and felt as if i had escaped from an ogre den
that the tragical fate of tom_loker also has too many time had its parallel there are living witnesses all over our land to testify
let it be remembered that in all southern state it is a principle of jurisprudence that no person of colored lineage can testify in a suit against a white and it will be easy to see that such a case may occur wherever there is a man whose passions outweigh his interests and a slave who has manhood or principle enough to resist his will
from the same source was derived the character of the planter simon_legree there is actually nothing to protect the slave life but the character of the master
fact too shocking to be contemplated occasionally force their way to the public ear and the comment that one often hears made on them is more shocking than the thing itself
it is said very likely such case may now and then occur but they are no sample of general practice
if the law of new england were so arranged that a master could now and then torture an apprentice to death would it be received with equal composure
would it be said these case are rare and no samples of general practice this injustice is an inherent one in the slave system it cannot exist without it
the public and shameless sale of beautiful mulatto and quadroon girl has acquired a notoriety from the incidents following the capture of the pearl
we extract the following from the speech of hon horace mann one of the legal counsel for the defendants in that case
he says in that company of seventy six persons who attempted in to escape from the district of columbia in the schooner pearl and whose officers i assisted in defending there were several young and healthy girl who had those peculiar attractions of form and feature which connoisseurs prize so highly
elizabeth russel was one of them she immediately fell into the slave trader fangs and was doomed for the new orleans market
they offered eighteen hundred dollar to redeem her and some there were who offered to give that would not have much left after the gift but the fiend of a slave trader was inexorable
she was despatched to new orleans but when about half way there god had mercy on her and smote her with death
the heart of those that saw her were touched with pity for her fate there were two girl named edmundson in the same company
when about to be sent to the same market an older sister went to the shambles to plead with the wretch who owned them for the love of god to spare his victims
he bantered her telling what fine dresses and fine furniture they would have yes she said that may do very well in this life but what will become of them in the next
they too were sent to new orleans but were afterwards redeemed at an enormous ransom and brought back is it not plain from this that the histories of emmeline and misse_cassy may have many counterparts
justice too obliges the author to state that the fairness of mind and generosity attributed to augustine_st_clare are not without a parallel as the following anecdote will show
a few year since a young southern gentleman was in cincinnati with a favorite servant who had been his personal attendant from a boy
the young man took advantage of this opportunity to secure his own freedom and fled to the protection of a quaker who was quite noted in affairs of this kind
he had always treated the slave with such indulgence and his confidence in his affection was such that he believed he must have been practised upon to induce him to revolt from him
he visited the quaker in high anger but being possessed of uncommon candor and fairness was soon quieted by his arguments and representations
it was a side of the subject which he never had heard never had thought on and he immediately told the quaker that if his slave would to his own face say that it was his desire to be free he would liberate him
an interview was forthwith procured and nathan was asked by his young master whether he had ever had any reason to complain of his treatment in any respect
the owner was exceedingly indignant no mas said nathan you ve always been good to me well then why do you want to leave me
mas may die and then who get me i rather be a free man after some deliberation the young master replied nathan in your place i think i should feel very much so myself
he immediately made him out free paper deposited a sum of money in the hand of the quaker to be judiciously used in assisting him to start in life and left a very sensible and kind letter of advice to the young man
the author hopes she has done justice to that nobility generosity and humanity which in many case characterize individuals at the south
you are free that letter was for some time in the writer hand such instances save us from utter despair of our kind
for many year of her life the author avoided all reading upon or allusion to the subject of slavery considering it as too painful to be inquired into and one which advancing light and civilization would certainly live down
but since the legislative act of when she heard with perfect surprise and consternation christian and humane people actually recommending the remanding escaped fugitives into slavery as a duty binding on good
she heard on all hand from kind compassionate and estimable people in the free state of the north deliberations and discussions as to what christian duty could be on this
head she could only think these man and christians cannot know what slavery is if they did such a question could never be open for discussion
but she asks any person who knows the world are such characters common anywhere citizens when and from this arose a desire to exhibit it in a living dramatic reality
she has endeavored to show it fairly in its best and its worst phases in its best aspect she has perhaps been successful but
oh who shall say what yet remains untold in that valley and shadow of death that lies the other side
to you generous noble minded man and woman of the south you whose virtue and magnanimity and purity of character are the greater for the severer trial it has
have you not in your own secret soul in your own private conversings felt that there are woes and evils in this accursed system far beyond what are here shadowed or can be shadowed
encountered to you is her appeal can it be otherwise is man ever a creature to be trusted with wholly irresponsible power
and does not the slave system by denying the slave all legal right of testimony make every individual owner an irresponsible despot
if there is as we admit a public sentiment among you man of honor justice and humanity is there not also another kind of public sentiment among the ruffian the brutal and debased
and cannot the ruffian the brutal the debased by slave law own just as many slave as the best and purest
can anybody fail to make the inference what the practical result will be are the honorable the just the high minded and compassionate the majority anywhere in this world
but a slave trade as systematic as ever was carried on on the coast of africa is an inevitable attendant and result of american slavery
the writer has given only a faint shadow a dim picture of the anguish and despair that are at this very moment riving thousands of heart shattering thousands of family and driving a helpless and sensitive race to frenzy and despair
there are those living who know the mother whom this accursed traffic has driven to the murder of their child and themselves seeking in death a shelter from woes more dreaded than death
nothing of tragedy can be written can be spoken can be conceived that equals the frightful reality of scenes daily and hourly acting on our shores beneath the shadow of american law and the shadow of the cross of jesus_christ
and now man and woman of america is this a thing to be trifled with apologized for and passed over in silence
farmers of massachusetts of new hampshire of vermont of connecticut who read this book by the blaze of your winter evening fire strong hearted generous sailors and ship owners of maine is this a thing for you to countenance and encourage
brave and generous man of new york farmers of rich and joyous ohio and ye of the wide prairie state answer is this a thing for you to protect and countenance
and you mother of america you who have learned by the cradles of your own child to love and feel for all mankind by the sacred love you bear your child by your joy in his beautiful spotless infancy by the motherly pity and tenderness with which you guide his growing year by the anxieties of his education by the prayers you breathe for his soul eternal good i beseech you pity the mother who has all your affections and not one legal right to protect guide or educate the child of her bosom
by the sick hour of your child by those dying eye which you can never forget by those last cries that wrung your heart when you could neither help nor save by the desolation of that empty cradle that silent nursery i beseech you pity those mother that are constantly made childless by the american slave trade
the slave trade is now by american law considered as piracy and its heart break and its horrors can they be told and say mother of america is this a thing to be defended sympathized with passed over in silence
do you say that the people of the free state have nothing to do with it and can do nothing would to god this were true
the people of the free state have defended encouraged and participated and are more guilty for it before god than the south in that they have not the apology of education or custom
if the mother of the free state had all felt as they should in time past the sons of the free state would not have been the holders and proverbially the hardest master of slave the sons of the free state would not have connived at the extension of slavery in our national body the sons of the free state would not as they do trade the soul and body of man as an equivalent to money in their mercantile dealings
there are multitudes of slave temporarily owned and sold again by merchants in northern cities and shall the whole guilt or obloquy of slavery fall only on the south
northern man northern mother northern christians have something more to do than denounce their brethren at the south they have to look to the evil among themselves
but it is not true but what can any individual do of that every individual can judge there is one thing that every individual can do they can see to it that they feel right
an atmosphere of sympathetic influence encircles every human being and the man or woman who feels strongly healthily and justly on the great interests of humanity is a constant benefactor to the human race
see then to your sympathies in this matter are they in harmony with the sympathies of jesus_christ or are they swayed and perverted by the sophistries of worldly policy
christian man and woman of the north still further you have another power you can pray do you believe in prayer or has it become an indistinct apostolic tradition
and pray for those distressed christians whose whole chance of religious improvement is an accident of trade and sale from whom any adherence to the morals of christianity is in many case an impossibility unless they have given them from above the courage and grace of martyrdom
on the shores of our free state are emerging the poor shattered broken remnants of family man and woman escaped by miraculous providences from the surges of slavery feeble in knowledge and in many case infirm in moral constitution from a system which confounds and confuses every principle of christianity and morality
you pray for the heathen abroad pray also for the heathen at home but still more they come to seek a refuge among you they come to seek education knowledge christianity
does not every american christian owe to the african race some effort at reparation for the wrongs that the american nation has brought upon them
what do you owe to these poor unfortunates oh christians shall the door of churches and school house be shut upon them
shall the church of jesus_christ hear in silence the taunt that is thrown at them and shrink away from the helpless hand that they stretch out and by her silence encourage the cruelty that would chase them from our borders
if it must be so the country will have reason to tremble when it remembers that the fate of nations is in the hand of one who is very pitiful and of tender compassion
shall state arise and shake them out if it must be so it will be a mournful spectacle do you say we dont want them here let them go to africa
that the providence of god has provided a refuge in africa is indeed a great and noticeable fact but that is no reason why the church of jesus_christ should throw off that responsibility to this outcast race which her profession demands of her
to fill up liberia with an ignorant inexperienced half barbarized race just escaped from the chains of slavery would be only to prolong for ages the period of struggle and conflict which attends the inception of new enterprises
let the church of the north receive these poor sufferers in the spirit of jesus_christ receive them to the educating advantages of christian republican society and schools until they have attained to somewhat of a moral and intellectual maturity and then assist them in their passage to those shores where they may put in practice the lessons they have learned in america
there is a body of man at the north comparatively small who have been doing this and as the result this country has already seen examples of man formerly slave who have rapidly acquired property reputation and education
talent has been developed which considering the circumstances is certainly remarkable and for moral traits of honesty kindness tenderness of feeling for heroic efforts and self denials endured for the ransom of brethren and friend yet in slavery they have been remarkable to a degree that considering the influence under which they were born is surprising
the writer has lived for many year on the frontier line of slave state and has had great opportunities of observation among those who formerly were slave
they have been in her family as servant and in default of any other school to receive them she has in many case had them instructed in a family school with her own child
she has also the testimony of missionaries among the fugitives in canada in coincidence with her own experience and her deductions with regard to the capabilities of the race are encouraging in the highest degree
there is nothing that they are not willing to give or do to have their child instructed and so far as the writer has observed herself or taken the testimony of teachers among them they are remarkably intelligent and quick to learn
the first desire of the emancipated slave generally is for education the results of schools founded for them by benevolent individuals in cincinnati fully establish this
the author gives the following statement of fact on the authority of professor e stowe then of lane seminary ohio with regard to emancipated slave now resident in cincinnati given to show the capability of the race even without any very particular assistance or encouragement
the initial letter alone are given they are all residents of cincinnati furniture maker twenty year in the city worth ten thousand dollar all his own earnings a baptist
full black stolen from africa sold in new orleans been free fifteen year paid for himself six hundred dollar a farmer owns several farms in indiana presbyterian probably worth fifteen or twenty thousand dollar all earned by himself
full black dealer in real estate worth thirty thousand dollar about forty year old free six year paid eighteen hundred dollar for his family member of the baptist church received a legacy from his master which he has taken good care of and increased
full black coal dealer about thirty year old worth eighteen thousand dollar paid for himself twice being once defrauded to the amount of sixteen hundred dollar made all his money by his own efforts much of it while a slave hiring his time of his master and doing business for himself a fine gentlemanly fellow
three fourths black barber and waiter from kentucky nineteen year free paid for self and family over three thousand dollar deacon in the baptist church
three fourths black white washer from kentucky nine year free paid fifteen hundred dollar for self and family recently died aged sixty worth six thousand dollar
professor stowe says with all these except i have been for some year personally acquainted and make my statements from my own knowledge
g g the writer well remembers an aged colored woman who was employed as a washerwoman in her father family
she was a remarkably active and capable young woman and by her industry and thrift and the most persevering self denial raised nine hundred dollar for her husband freedom which she paid as she raised it into the hand of his master
the daughter of this woman married a slave she yet wanted a hundred dollar of the price when he died she never recovered any of the money
these are but few fact among multitudes which might be adduced to show the self denial energy patience and honesty which the slave has exhibited in a state of freedom
and let it be remembered that these individuals have thus bravely succeeded in conquering for themselves comparative wealth and social position in the face of every disadvantage and discouragement
the colored man by the law of ohio cannot be a voter and till within a few year was even denied the right of testimony in legal suits with the white
in all state of the union we see man but yesterday burst from the shackles of slavery who by a self educating force which cannot be too much admired have risen to highly respectable stations in society
nor are these instances confined to the state of ohio pennington among clergymen douglas and ward among editors are well known instances
if this persecuted race with every discouragement and disadvantage have done thus much how much more they might do if the christian church would act towards them in the spirit of her lord
this is an age of the world when nations are trembling and convulsed a mighty influence is abroad surging and heaving the world as with an earthquake
and is america safe every nation that carries in its bosom great and unredressed injustice has in it the elements of this last convulsion
for what is this mighty influence thus rousing in all nations and languages those groanings that cannot be uttered for man freedom and equality
is not this power the spirit of him whose kingdom is yet to come and whose will to be done on earth as it is in heaven
for that day shall burn as an oven and he shall appear as a swift witness against those that oppress the hireling in his wages the widow and the fatherless and that turn aside the stranger in his right and he shall break in pieces the oppressor
o church of jesus_christ read the signs of the time but who may abide the day of his appearing are not these dread word for a nation bearing in her bosom so mighty an injustice
every time that you pray that the kingdom of jesus_christ may come can you forget that prophecy associates in dread fellowship the day of vengeance with the year of his redeemed
christians a day of grace is yet held out to us both north and south have been guilty before god and the christian church has a heavy account to answer
not by combining together to protect injustice and cruelty and making a common capital of sin is this union to be saved but by repentance justice and mercy for not surer is the eternal law by which the millstone sinks in the ocean than that stronger law by which injustice and cruelty shall bring on nations the wrath of almighty god
